## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA_dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the central object of chemical rate laws. The most natural domain is chemical reaction kinetics, where rate expressions are derived from elementary steps, often involving power laws, exponential dependences, and combinations that capture saturation, autocatalysis, or time-dependent deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A (rate directly proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate, order = c1)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (linear ODE to equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic / logistic type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self‑accelerating then decelerating)
- Prout‑Tompkins nucleation-growth: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (solid‑state kinetics, branching reaction)
- Elovich chemisorption: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * A) (rate decays exponentially with amount adsorbed/reacted)
- Time‑dependent first‑order: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation / decay of rate constant)
- Mixed‑order recombination: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first‑ and second‑order paths)
- Avrami‑type time‑power law: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * (c2 - A) (phase transformation kinetics with time‑dependent nucleation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Zero‑order kinetics: constant rate term indicates reaction rate independent of concentration, often due to surface saturation or constant supply.
- First‑order kinetics: linear dependence on A leads to exponential decay of reactant; typical for unimolecular elementary steps.
- Higher integer order: rate proportional to A**2 or A**3 suggests elementary bimolecular or termolecular collisions.
- Fractional order: power‑law A**c1 with non‑integer c1 indicates complex mechanism, diffusion‑limited, or fractal kinetics.
- Reversible reaction: combination of a constant term and negative linear term (c0 - c1*A) models relaxation to equilibrium.
- Autocatalytic / logistic: rate as product A*(c1‑A) captures self‑acceleration followed by slowing when reactant is depleted.
- Heterogeneous / solid‑state kinetics: product of powers of A and (c2‑A) (Prout‑Tompkins) represents branching nucleation and growth.
- Decaying rate constant: exponential factor exp(‑c1*t) multiplying concentration indicates catalyst deactivation or loss of active sites.
- Chemisorption / Elovich: exponential dependence on A, dA_dt ∝ exp(‑c1*A), yields logarithmic time law typical for surface reactions.
- Non‑autonomous rate: explicit t**c1 term in the rate law suggests external time‑dependent influence (e.g., temperature ramp, changing illumination).

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

This simplifies to: `f(A) = -c*A² + d*A²/(e*A⁴ + 1)` — a rational function of A only (no t dependence).

Key structural features of GT:
- It's a function of A only (no t)
- It has a term `-c*A²` (polynomial)
- It has a term `d*A²/(e*A⁴ + 1)` (rational function)
- Combined: `(-c*A²*(e*A⁴+1) + d*A²) / (e*A⁴+1)` = `A²*(-c*e*A⁴ - c + d) / (e*A⁴+1)`
- = `A²*(d-c) / (e*A⁴+1) - c*e*A⁶/(e*A⁴+1)`

Let me compute: d-c = 0.4599 - 0.1900 = 0.2699, c*e = 0.1900*0.7498 = 0.1424

So GT = `(0.2699*A² - 0.1424*A⁶) / (0.7498*A⁴ + 1)`

Or equivalently: GT = `A²*(0.2699 - 0.1424*A⁴) / (0.7498*A⁴ + 1)`

Now let me check each candidate for structural equivalence.

**Candidate 1:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2 + c3 + c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6 + c7*t) + 1)`
Contains log and exp terms, and t dependence. Setting c4=0 removes the log term, leaving `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3`. Setting c1=2, c0=0, c3=0 gives `c2*A²`. But GT is not just `c2*A²`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Contains log terms. GT has no logarithmic components. Cannot match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `A**6*c0/(A**5+c1) + A**5*c2/(A**5+c1) + A**5*c3*exp(A*c4)/(A**5+c1) + A**5*c5/(A**5+c1) + A*c6/(A**5+c1) + c7/(A**5+c1) + c8*exp(A*c4)/(A**5+c1)`

= `(A⁶*c0 + A⁵*(c2+c5)) / (A⁵+c1)`

GT = `(α*A² - β*A⁶) / (γ*A⁴+1)` — denominator is A⁴+const, not A⁵+const. Different rational structure. Cannot match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** Contains log terms only. Cannot match rational function. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6`

Setting c0=0, c4=0, c6=0: `A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3)`. With c1=2: `c2*A²/(A²+c3)`. 

GT needs `A²/(A⁴+const)` type term plus `-A²` term. Let me check if `A*c0 + A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) + c6` can match.

Setting c1=4: `c0*A + c2*A⁴/(A⁴+c3) + c6`. This gives a constant approaching c2+c6 for large A. But GT ~ -c*A² for large A. Need A² term.

Setting c1=2: `c0*A + c2*A²/(A²+c3) + c6`. For large A, this ~ c0*A + c2 + c6, linear growth. GT ~ -c*A², quadratic decay. Cannot match. [NO MATCH]
